Discussion Title: Has Religion Been a Good Thing for Humanity?

1. Religion has been a good thing for humankind.
1.1. Pro: Religion has created valuable moral codes and philosophical frameworks.
1.1.1. Pro: Our understanding of "good" and "humanity" are mostly grounded in religion. Saying religion has not been good is a contradiction because religion has defined the meaning of "good" in our development as a species.
1.1.1.1. Con: The more we learn about other animals, particularly social species, the more we understand that moral and ethical behaviors are not simply human characteristics.  And given that only humans have religion, it would be incorrect to say what we understand as good or human is grounded in religion.  Those without religion understand what is or is not good, and it has more to do with our instincts as an empathizing social species.    [Finding Morality in Animals](https://greatergood.berkeley.edu/article/item/morality_animals)
1.1.1.2. Con: This amounts to "we're-right-because-we-say-we're-right". It's evidence that religion is bad for humanity, because it amounts to letting the few tell the many what they have to do and what they can't do, under threat not just of being in the wrong but of eternal damnation.
1.1.1.3. Con: Religion is not the only source of ethics, [secular ethics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secular_ethics) exists and can be used to evaluate whether or not religion is good this is not a contradiction.
1.1.1.4. Con: If moral codes were universally originated in religion there would be more homogeneity between cultures and not countless different religious denominations across the world.
1.1.1.5. Pro: The very notion of "good" would not exist in the absence of religion, without a [transcendent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_and_evil#Transcendental_realism) instance, beyond human reach.
1.1.1.5.1. Con: Good and bad are subjective terms that make up a dichotomy. They are often defined by each other, not by religion. Things are good only in comparison to bad things and vice versa. This does not require religion to work.
1.1.1.5.2. Con: Since humans are in any case those who interpret and apply the transcendental notion of good, even if this is sanctioned by a higher power, its application is bound to abuse or misuse, in the same manner that any human construct on morality and ethics is.
1.1.1.5.2.1. Con: Human judgement is indeed imperfect. Yet, the notion of good remains the same irrespective of any human judgement. This is why, for example, in Christian Bible it is said not to judge. This is the atribute of the divinity.
1.1.1.6. Con: Perceptions of "good" and "humanity" could have been derived naturally or elsewhere, and then transcribed into religion.
1.1.1.6.1. Pro: There is no tangible and specific evidence that what is deemed good or bad is actually based on religion.
1.1.1.6.2. Pro: [Natural morality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_morality) is the moral philosophy describing how we arrived at the morals we currently possess through evolution and thus such morals help us survive as individuals and as a species.
1.1.2. Pro: Religions provided, for centuries, common behavioral guidelines for the society, enabling an organized and peaceful coexistence \(what constitutions and legal codes do today\).
1.1.2.1. Con: History has been quite the [opposite of peaceful](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_wars) for virtually all of recorded human existence. Peaceful coexistence has simply not been a feature of reality.
1.1.2.2. Con: Modern propagation of news gives the unintentional impression that there was a good-old-days by spreading bad news far more efficiently than in the past and far more efficiently than the good news progress, much of it secular or scientific, has wrought. Rather than peaceful coexistence there was relative ignorance of war, murders, theft, bigotry etc.
1.1.2.3. Pro: Religion helps people focus on the present by finding peace in God's will and trusting in his plans and guidance. This inner peace permeates outwards and reduces conflict.
1.1.2.3.1. Con: Peace can imply complacency in which one simply stands by and allows atrocities to occur to themselves and others. Things such as the [bystander effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bystander_effect) illustrate just how complacent humans already are without a shift in attitude of only focusing on the present and on inner piece.
1.1.2.3.2. Pro: Many religions hold peace and tolerance as core values
1.1.2.3.2.1. Pro: Christianity instills values of peace and non-violence.
1.1.2.3.2.1.1. Pro: Christianity [compels](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Exodus+20&version=NIV) its followers not to kill, commit adultery, or steal.
1.1.2.3.2.1.1.1. Con: Contemporary law is not based at all on the 10 commandments. The first four are about god and the sabbath none of which appears in contemporary  western law. Honoring your parents may be expected but is not required. Killing is permitted under certain circumstances \(self defense\). Adultery and coveting goods are not illegal either. Theft and perjury are all that remain.
1.1.2.3.2.1.1.1.1. Pro: Even [perjury has been watered down to varying degrees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perjury). Generally it can only be illegal if you're lying to the police or under oath.
1.1.2.3.2.1.2. Pro: One of the 10 commandments is "thou shalt not kill".
1.1.2.3.2.1.3. Con: Religion has preached intolerance for centuries and persecuted people for just as long, people typically do not want to be persecuted and so it would seem that at least not all religions hold that you should treat all others as you would want to be treated.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1. Pro: Religion has historically had to catch up and modify its morality to fit the changing secular standards. If its moral code was truly beneficial it wouldn't have to play catch up to secular ethics.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.1. Pro: The [Bible](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Bible_and_slavery) was used as both an argument for and against [slavery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_views_on_slavery).
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.2. Pro: Christian responses to domestic abuse have been catching up to secular standards over the past 40 years. [Many pastors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_and_domestic_violence#Responses_to_abuse) have said and many continue to say that they would never advise a women to leave an abusive husband, and many advise forgiveness and enduring.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.2.1. Pro: Recently church leaders such as the Pope and bishops have openly condemned this behavior and with more women pastors entering the ranks the responses are finally catching up to secular standards.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3. Pro: The [Catholic church molestation scandals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church_sexual_abuse_cases) show that until pressed by secular authorities religious ones are content to hide their crimes.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3.1. Pro: A report estimated about [7% of clergy](https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2017/sep/13/catholic-sexual-abuse-partly-caused-by-celibacy-and-secrecy-report-finds) had abused children between about 1950 and 2000.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3.2. Con: The Congregation of the [Servants of the Paraclete](http://mtcarmelrenewalcenter.org/about/) was founded in the 1940's by Fr. Gerald Fitzgerald to expose and help prevent child sexual abuse by the clergy.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3.2.1. Con: Fitzgerald started to assist priests dealing with substance abuse but soon began receiving priests who had sexually abused minors. He did not bring them to justice and was [against secular treatments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_of_the_Servants_of_the_Paraclete) like psychiatry and psychology.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3.2.2. Con: Fitzgerald recommended some priests to be laicized but, in general, most bishops chose to [ignore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_of_the_Servants_of_the_Paraclete) his recommendations and kept employing priests with sexual abuse history.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3.2.3. Con: The center was [closed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congregation_of_the_Servants_of_the_Paraclete) in the 1990s as the result of lawsuits over priests who had molested children while staying at the center or after being treated at the facility.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3.2.4. Con: Abusive priests from all over the US where brought to the Monastery run by the Servants of the Paracletes since 1947. Very often, those priests were released to work with [non-white and poor communities](https://rewire.news/religion-dispatches/2018/08/27/from-pa-to-new-mexico-colonialism-and-the-crisis-inside-the-crisis-of-catholic-sexual-abuse/) and very often sexual abuses continued. In that sense, the church disposed of abusive priest in predominately white and mid-western communities to bring them to poorer and brown communities, without ever truly eradicating sexual abuse.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.3.2.4.1. Pro: Fr. Edward Graff \(included in the [Pennsylvania grand jury report](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/acts-of-faith/wp/2018/08/14/pennsylvania-grand-jury-report-on-sex-abuse-in-catholic-church-will-list-hundreds-of-accused-predator-priests/?utm_term=.c90e5d6dca61)\) was moved from Allentown where the report alleges “raped scores of children” to the Monastery. Eventually, in 1980, he was released and worked in Texas and New Mexico until being arrested for [sexually abusing](https://rewire.news/religion-dispatches/2018/08/27/from-pa-to-new-mexico-colonialism-and-the-crisis-inside-the-crisis-of-catholic-sexual-abuse/) a minor. In the investigation, it was discovered he would employ and potentially abuse young and poor Hispanic youth. He died in prison before trial.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.4. Pro: The Catholic church preached as doctrine that the Jews were collectively responsible for [deicide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_deicide). This belief fostered two millennia of antisemitism and was only [repudiated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_deicide#Repudiation) and removed as doctrine in 1962 during the second Vatican Council. This antisemitism was part of the environment that allowed Hitler's rise.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5. Con: Secular and religious ethics are vastly intertwined. In religious doctrines you are asked to do good and be good. This doesn't mean that religion introduced these ethics but it did help propagate them.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.1. Con: While the set of secular morals/ethics can change and be added to as we learn, religion does not change. That makes religion a barrier to morals and ethics beyond those it subscribes to.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.1.1. Pro: The bible ends in [68AD](https://ichthys.com/mail-Bible%20chrono.htm), at the end of Revelations, and was finished by Apostle John in [95AD](https://www.biblica.com/resources/bible-faqs/when-was-the-bible-written/) at least 1804 years before any currently living person was born. Nothing was added when we learnt to treat women and men equally, nor when we learnt that cowering is not "yes" and "no" is relevant in marriage, nor when we learnt to treat each others' sexual preferences equally.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.1.1.1. Pro: If there is a God he won't have overlooked the morals the bible does. Remember the [story](https://truthbook.com/stories/funny-god/the-drowning-man): A man on a roof in a flood who waits for God to save him and turns down three forms of salvation before drowning. Then God tells him that he sent those three. Religion has ignored much that it could have seen as messages from God over the last 1800 years. There's been more than a rowboat, a motorboat and a helicopter in that time but religion is still not seeing the signs.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.2. Con: Secular ethics and religious ethics are distinguished by where they come from. A framework of secular ethics may have the same exact tenets as a religious one and yet be derived in a completely different way. It is also possible for them to have completely differing tenets. The definition of secular ethics is that it is not derived from religion thus the term secular. So without completely redefining the terms we are using it is impossible to say that they are the same.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.3. Pro: Even if the [Golden Rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Rule#Ancient_Egypt) \(treating other as ones would wish to be treated\) was not invented by Christianity, Christianity did make it popular.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.3.1. Con: Religion takes claim of things without regard for the original source; often absorbing aspects of subjected people's culture, as a mean to further control and dominate them.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.4. Pro: [Scholasticism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scholasticism) acted as a bridge between Greek and Roman knowledge and Christian theology, as a way of teaching that [focused](https://www.britannica.com/topic/Western-philosophy/Medieval-philosophy) on "logic, dialectic, and all the scientific disciplines known at the time".
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.5.4.1. Con: The fact that religious people did logical things does not imply that they did it because they were religious.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.6. Con: The higher rate of change of secular ethics does not make them more true. It just means religious ethics move more slowly. This could be a good thing, when the common opinion is changed for the worse.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.6.1. Con: Most religions' primary texts are finalized at some point. After that their ethics don't move slowly—they don't move at all.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.7. Pro: [Blasphemy laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blasphemy_law) have been overturned slowly over time and some still exist. This runs counter to the secular ideal of free speech and is slowly being stripped away in the western world.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.8. Pro: Religion still to this day condemns the morality of the LGBT community, a practice modern western society condemns as bigotry.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.8.1. Pro: Religion can be used as a protective barrier to further discriminatory, or harmful views that would otherwise be seen as violations of rights. For example, refusing to provide services for LGBT+ individuals on the basis of exercising religious freedom.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.9. Pro: Religion moves too slow in regard to society therefore their values are too archaic to be useful
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.1.9.1. Con: Martin Luther Kings famously [analogised](https://stanfordfreedomproject.com/multi-media-essays-on-freedom/the-biblical-exodus-in-the-rhetoric-of-martin-luther-king/) the struggle of the civil rights movement to the biblical story of [Exodus](http://videri.org/index.php?title=Martin_Luther_King_and_the_Rhetoric_of_Freedom:_The_Exodus_Narrative_in_America%27s_Struggle_for_Civil_Rights), proving that religion is not archaic if recontextualised correctly.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2. Pro: The moral codes often found in religious texts have been the cause of many social injustices including the persecution of homosexuals, people of colour and women.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.1. Pro: To give some idea of the scope of this issue, including persecution of those perceived as atheists: The percentage of us who are white male heterosexual Christians \(using this group not as definitive, but only to get us in the right ballpark\) is very low, so the vast majority of us are potential targets.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.2. Pro: Religion often condemns [homosexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexuality_and_religion).
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3. Pro: Religion has tried to control women's bodies by banning abortion, birth control and contraception.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1. Con: Opposing abortion is a testament to the preservation of life. Abortion can be viewed as killing potential life.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1. Con: The preservation of life leads to overpopulation, which leads to famine, spreading of diseases, and many other causes of death. So saving some lives indirectly kills much more lives. [Overpopulation effects.](http://www.everythingconnects.org/overpopulation-effects.html)
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1. Con: The preservation of life has a [marginal effect](https://www.conserve-energy-future.com/causes-effects-solutions-of-overpopulation.php) on population growth. Other factors to take into consideration are: the decrease in mortality rates, the overcoming of poverty, advancements in fertility treatments, immigration and the lack of family planning.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1. Con: Religiosity has [decreased](http://www.cbc.ca/news/world/do-countries-lose-religion-as-they-gain-wealth-1.1310451) internationally, especially in developed countries, and many believers do not follow every religious teaching, yet if most of the world’s population did, overpopulation could be a bigger problem.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: The [Roman Catholic Church](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/christianity/christianethics/contraception_1.shtml) refuses artificial methods of contraception; many [Hindus](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/hinduism/hinduethics/contraception.shtml) are unlikely to use contraception; in [Orthodox Judaism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_views_on_contraception), birth control is not acceptable or only to use in limited circumstances and although [Islam](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/islam/islamethics/contraception.shtml) allows contraception, more conservative leaders campaign against it.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Opposing birth control and contraception can be viewed as advocating against promiscuity.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Regardless of how one views it the consequences are real and can be shown.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.1.1.2. Con: Religion has made promiscuity a bad thing, because if women had multiple partners the filiation link couldn't be established. By forcing monogamy \(at least for women \) on humanity , religion portrayed "promiscuity" as a bad thing. But one could see it as a very natural thing, to respond to one's desires.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.1.1.3. Con: Opposing birth control also increases venereal disease.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.1.1.4. Con: When contraception is prohibited even between married spouses, promiscuity is not the key element in its prohibition.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.2. Con: -> See discussion #9226: Global overpopulation is a myth.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.2.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.2. Pro: Killing potential life is immoral
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.1.1.1.1.1.1.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3. Con: Control does not imply harm.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.1. Con: "Forced conversions" implies harm would befall the converted if they would not convert. Therefore, this conversion is harmful to the well-being of the converted.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.2. Pro: Control is not necessarily harming people. [Leadership and followship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_leadership_theory) can be beneficial to both parties. Power is sometimes viewed as only tyrannical control over the populations, but we often forget the benevolent and caring side of organized social structures.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.2.1. Con: Even if control was beneficial for a person, it would still be unjustified. Each person should have the right to decide how they will live their life, and noone should be able to make that decision for them. To decide otherwise is the beginning of tyranny.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.2.1.1. Con: People can value security over freedom and therefore feel happier when they don't have to choose everything themselves. Excessive choice is tyranny to some.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.2.2. Pro: Traditionally, a [democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy) is a way for the followers to elect the leaders. People choose and respect the most competent people that they can trust to rule over them and represent their views on large scale issues.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.2.2.1. Con: Democracy is a very inefficient type of government structure. It is maintained as a social luxury, not for its merit.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.3. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.2.1.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4. Pro: Religious social control can be and most often is consensually chosen by the believers themselves, particularly among converts.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.1. Con: If the religion has control over public policy and uses it to exert social control, then non-believers will also be forced to adhere nonconsensually to the control created. [Pew Article on views on abortion](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2018/01/22/american-religious-groups-vary-widely-in-their-views-of-abortion/)[Views on homosexuality](http://www.pewforum.org/religious-landscape-study/views-about-homosexuality/)
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.2. Con: Religious control uses emotion and faith which ignore reason. This makes the religion itself and the individuals less able to rationally evaluate social impacts or structures. A tipping point emerges when a religion cannot assess appropriate impacts within a larger group and are outcast as cult.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.2.1. Pro: The problem is more profound when the religion wields too much influence for it to be outcast.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3. Con: Being born and indoctrinated into a faith is not voluntary. Moreover several religions place severe consequences on those who leave.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.1. Pro: If you leave Islam in certain countries you will die. If you leave Jehova's witnesses you will never speak to your family again. Same with the Amish. But more importantly you did not choose to have the religion forced on you as a child and it may be so deep in your brain that you could never escape.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.2. Pro: [Religious Trauma Syndrome \(RTS\)](http://www.babcp.com/Review/RTS-Trauma-from-Leaving-Religion.aspx) “is a function of both the chronic abuses of harmful religion and the impact of severing one’s connection with one’s faith” and can be compared to a combination of PTSD and Complex PTSD.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.3. Pro: Religions are routinely introduced to children who are too young to make an informed choice.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.3.1. Con: Children are capable of choice, but the degree to which they can make an informed and/or rational decision will vary from not at all, through not enough, to a minority who are as capable of making a decision as an adult.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.3.2. Pro: [Circumcision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circumcision#Cultures_and_religions) is performed by Jews on the eighth day of life.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.3.3. Pro: The [First Communion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Communion) is normally received around the ages of 7 to 10  after a period or [cathequesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catechesis) \(education\). And [Confirmation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confirmation#cite_note-28), the time when the believer really gives consent, also happens when children are young or in their mid-teens.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.3.4. Pro: Catholic parents [baptise](http://www.annunciationevv.org/Guidelines-for-Baptism) their children when they are babies and thus introduce them into the Catholic faith when they cannot consent.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.3.4. Pro: Hasidic Jews are [indoctrinated](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/05/21/ex-hasidim-life-stories_n_7343084.html) from a young age, often poorly educated \(with lack of English skills\) and pressured to have and provide for big families at really young ages. Those who try to live [secularly](http://www.nycreligion.info/leaving-ultraorthodox-judaism/) are often completely [rejected](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/30/magazine/the-high-price-of-leaving-ultra-orthodox-life.html) and, in many cases, their religious communities fight to keep custody of their [children](https://www.refinery29.com/2017/10/177040/netflix-one-of-us-orthodox-jewish-women-abuse-etty?bucketed=true).
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.4.4. Con: Through history, most often than not religion social control is imposed. Nowadays it is imposed by social stigma in some countries.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.5. Con: Forcing women to continue their pregnancy and give birth may be harmful for the woman. Also, having to raise an unplanned child in a difficult economical or social environment can be a source of pain, such as starvation.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.5.1. Pro: Fetuses do not have a conscious mind capable of experiencing pain and suffering. Pain reception only develops well into the [third trimester](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/when-does-consciousness-arise/) of pregnancy.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.5.2. Pro: As the fetus is a biological extension of the mother, it is up to her do with it what she sees fit.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.5.3. Con: Not all religious people view abortion as wrong.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.5.3.1. Con: In a lot of cases, even if individual believers do not think abortion is wrong, their religious teachings say otherwise.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.5.3.1.1. Pro: The [Roman Catholic Church](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/christianity/christianethics/abortion_1.shtml#h2) considers an abortion "a grave moral wrong"; in [Sikhism](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/sikhism/sikhethics/abortion.shtml) abortion if forbiden; [Hinduism](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/hinduism/hinduethics/abortion_1.shtml) is opposed to it, except where it is necessary to save the mother; [Islam](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/islam/islamethics/abortion_1.shtml) regards abortion as wrong and forbidden though with vital exceptions and [Judaism](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/judaism/jewishethics/abortion_1.shtml) only permits it for serious reasons.
1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.3.3.5.3.2. 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1. Con: Even if it currently is impossible to determine if increased secularization causes more development, empirical evidence seems to support that more development does cause religiosity to decline.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1. Pro: Research points that religious belief declines in [economically developed countries](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/1069397111402465) with “greater existential security, including income security \(income equality and redistribution via welfare states\) and improved health”.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: Among those more [educated](http://www.pewforum.org/2017/04/26/in-america-does-more-education-equal-less-religion/), there is a tendency to have higher levels of [non belief](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/the-human-beast/201005/why-atheism-will-replace-religion) or to, at least, hold religious beliefs with less certainty.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: Some studies show a negative correlation between [intelligence](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/1088868313497266?journalCode=psra) and religiosity, possibly explained by the fact that intelligent people are less likely to conform to dogma and tend to adopt a [analytic](http://science.sciencemag.org/content/336/6080/493) way of thinking.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: These studies may not take into account other variables. Since many positive social conditions \(education, urbanization, income, etc.\) also happen to be correlated with loss of religion, the link could be explained more by those causes than by intelligence and religion themselves.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.1.2. Con: Correlation does not indicate causation. Education could just as easily be structured in a way that attracts non-religious people.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.2. Con: Statistics show that [birth rates decrease](https://www.forbes.com/sites/currentevents/2012/10/16/warning-bell-for-developed-countries-declining-birth-rates/#7ba9e8963641) to dangerous levels in those same countries. Perhaps a decline in religious belief is not a good thing.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.3. Pro: As scientific knowledge allows to reduce [uncertainty](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/nigel-barber/why-atheism-to-replace-re_b_903653.html), in [democracies](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/the-human-beast/201005/why-atheism-will-replace-religion) with strong economies and welfare provisions, people find less need to deal with the uncertainty of the future through religion.
1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.4. Con: The cause of this trend could be that religion is less needed in economically developed countries; not that religion stagnates economic growth. Wealthy, comfortable people have little use for a theology that promises rewards in the afterlife. The impoverished, however, may find significant value in religious teachings telling them that human value is not measured by money, and that rewards await them in heaven for living a good life on earth.

1.1.16.7. Pro: [Kantian ethics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kantian_ethics) is a godless version of deontology, which proposes categorical imperatives. The requirement for these imperatives is that they should lead to good outcomes if followed by all people, in all circumstances. It also stresses the need to treat conscious beings as ends in their own right, and not means to lead to something greater.
1.1.16.7.1. Con: Kantian morality has been [criticized](https://courses.lumenlearning.com/sanjacinto-philosophy/chapter/kantian-ethics-criticisms/) as self-contradictory, and have presented a number of cases in which the Formula of Universal Law either provides no meaningful answer or gives an obviously wrong answer.
1.1.16.7.2. Con: Kantian ethics is useless in a practical sense since it requires people to behave as if everyone follows the same rules since every action must weighed as if it was based on a universal rule. In practice people do not all behave this way and making choices based on a hypothetical world that does not actually exist will lead to many things traditionally viewed as awful.
1.1.16.7.2.1. Con: Kant believed that the maxims of the categorical imperative work because [human reason is innate](https://plato.stanford.edu/entries/kant-judgment/). The rules should work universally.
1.1.16.7.2.1.1. Con: [Studies](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4050437/) [have](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17128609) shown that our reasoning abilities are often impaired or affected by our emotions. Since our reason is subjected to emotional influence the perfect reasoning necessary for Kant's imperative to work universally is impossible.

Pro: For example, [Al-Ghazali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ghazali#Reception_of_his_work), who basically made the case that [philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ghazali#Incoherence_of_the_Philosophers) didn't work because it didn't show faith to be reasonable and failed to prove the existence of God.
1.1.21.1.2.6.1.1. Pro: [Ibn Rushd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Averroes), a rationalist, "[attempted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ghazali#Reception_of_his_work) to refute al-Ghazali's views, though the work was not well received in the Muslim community".
1.1.21.1.2.6.1.2. Pro: [Orientalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ghazali#Reception_of_his_work) scholars argued that Al-Ghazali caused a "decline in scientific advancement in Islam, due to his refutation of the new philosophies of his time".
1.1.21.1.3. Con: Believing without evidence is not always bad and faith can lead to beneficial outcomes.
1.1.21.1.3.1. Pro: Faith was an [important factor](https://cdn.americanprogress.org/wp-content/uploads/kf/rel_Bernard_Lafayette.pdf) in keeping the American Civil Rights movement together in the face of a concerted and powerful opposition.
1.1.21.1.3.1.1. Con: It's impossible to know that people would not have stepped up to lead had churches not done so.
1.1.21.1.3.1.1.1. Pro: We do know that there were a number of crucial atheist leaders in the movement, such as [A. Philip Randolph](https://www.bostonglobe.com/ideas/2012/03/03/great-atheists-civil-rights-movement/Dt3WqwHgZZYBapznnupmXL/story.html).
1.1.21.1.3.1.2. Con: Many of the [Churches themselves](https://archives.nbclearn.com/portal/site/k-12/flatview?cuecard=5041) did not participate, even as their congregations did.
1.1.21.1.3.1.3. Con: The religious narrative instilled in the movement diminished the role of other oppressed groups that the religious did not like and cemented religious influence in the black community.
1.1.21.1.3.1.3.1. Pro: [Homophobia](https://www.jstor.org/stable/41675211?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents) may be more prevalent in the African American community because of religious influences.
1.1.21.1.3.1.3.2. Pro: Certain components of religious practice, such as the attitude to money and education, can contribute to individuals remaining in or rising out of poverty. It is [argued](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/lisa-a-keister/religion-contributes-wealth-poverty_b_1069766.html) that Conservative Protestantism may help perpetuate poverty.
1.1.21.1.3.1.3.2.1. Con: The failure to provide [reparations](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2014/06/the-case-for-reparations/361631/) for the stolen wealth of slavery is a far more convincing explanation as to why this community may struggle with poverty.
1.1.21.1.3.2. Pro: Faith was a component in the Parliamentarian's struggle, and eventual victory, in the [English Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Civil_War).
1.1.21.1.3.2.1. Con: The monarchy of England was eventually restored and the leader of the rebellion [Oliver Cromwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell#Political_reputation) effectively made himself a dictator. This is not the kind of example to be used as a plus mark for religion. This is especially the case given that the monarchs were head of the [church of England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Church_of_England).
1.1.21.1.3.3. Con: A stopped clock is right twice a day.
1.1.21.1.3.4. Con: This might be true when there is not enough evidence available. However, the habit of believing without relying on evidence, which may be more common among the religious, makes it socially acceptable for people to ignore available evidence in favor of religious dogma.
1.1.21.1.3.5. Con: Getting hit by a car may have beneficial outcomes if the victim gets a massive settlement or if they somehow meet their future spouse as a result. This doesn't justify trying to get hit by a car or thinking it is not bad.
1.1.21.1.3.6. Con: Statistical coincidence ensures that sometimes believing without evidence is not bad, but it still usually is.
1.1.21.1.4. Con: Most of human experience is subjective, and religion is an appropriate way to process our experience where logic and empiricism cannot.
1.1.21.1.4.1. Con: Processing in this manner amounts to choosing to perceive "evil" instead of human nature, and choosing perceive misfortune as a "test from god". The failure isn't in logic or empiricism, it's in the beholder.
1.1.21.1.4.1.1. Pro: [Camus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Camus) called it a philosophical suicide.
1.1.21.1.4.2. Con: Religion is not only applied to experiences that logic and empiricism cannot process, as shown by constant clashes between religion and science. In every single case, religion holds back logic and empiricism.
1.1.21.1.4.2.1. Pro: Religions have destroyed knowledge in the name of their god countless times through history. Thus religions delayed advancement of humanity.
1.1.21.1.4.2.1.1. Pro: Religiously motivated [burning of books](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book_burning) was commonplace and continues to this day.
1.1.21.1.4.2.2. Pro: Religion has punished those with new \(and correct\) ideas setting back progress.  For [example](https://www.wikiwand.com/en/Galileo_affair), Galileo was imprisoned for writing in support of heliocentrism.
1.1.21.1.4.2.2.1. Con: The few examples of church opposition to scientific progress pale in comparison to its contribution to knowledge. For example, [Galileo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei#Controversy_over_heliocentrism) was not killed or even imprisoned, just put under temporary house arrest and allowed to continue his work.
1.1.21.1.4.2.2.1.1. Con: Being under house arrest does not seem a great endorsement of scientific discovery.
1.1.21.1.4.2.2.1.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.1.1.13.
1.1.21.1.4.2.2.1.3. Pro: Galileo was able [to continue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_affair#Trial_and_second_judgment,_1633) to work and publish under house arrest.
1.1.21.1.4.2.2.1.4. Con: Not killing someone does not count as a contribution towards science. It is rather not completely getting in the way of science but is still not a contribution.
1.1.21.1.4.2.3. Pro: The Catholic Church has [disputed the theory evolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolution_and_the_Catholic_Church).
1.1.21.1.4.2.4. Pro: Due to religious push back [stem cell research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stem_cell_laws_and_policy_in_the_United_States) was restricted and in part banned.
1.1.21.1.5. Pro: Religion creates a fantasy supposedly coexisting with reality. Then people prioritize this fantasy over reality in making decisions.
1.1.21.1.6. Pro: This has or will lead to hindering the logical thought process of seeking to understand and derive logical answers for any sort of claims
1.1.21.1.7. Pro: Religions provide an understanding of reality that is by nature further from the truth than that uncovered by scientific method. Human actions based on perceptions further from the truth yields worse results in areas such as medicine, engineering and restricts important perspectives on ourselves and our place in the universe \(e.g. timescale, evolution, our importance\).
1.1.21.1.8. Pro: Science has a method for weeding out the false, while religion does not.
1.1.21.1.9. Pro: Religion is a way to understand the Unknown, namely death and what happens to us after it. But, it requires no test, inquiry or research.
1.1.21.1.9.1. Pro: This allows for intellectual apathy in addressing problems, while attaching a person interest \(life after death/paradise\) to maintaining the faith.
1.1.21.1.10. Pro: Religion is permissive towards irrational/superstitious thinking and behaviors that then permeates other domains like politics
1.1.21.2. Con: The "rampant [forgiveness](https://nexusnovel.wordpress.com/2007/01/03/forgiveness-in-different-religions/) of sins" encourages sin.
1.1.21.3. Pro: Heaven and hell can be viewed as conceptions of your potential future. By designing your own heaven \(desired future\) to [strive for](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reward_system) and your own hell \(unwanted future\) [to avoid](http://integratedleader.com/articles/Importance_Fear.pdf), you are essentially [maximizing your motivation](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=e9pTz2_utU4) by using two different motivational systems.
1.1.21.3.1. Con: Heaven and Hell is a bipolar system based on fear, which suggest to do good things to avoid hell and not do bad things to go to heaven. It's an amoral system.
1.1.21.3.2. Con: However, "your own heaven" and "your own hell" are not what religion promote. Religions generally preempt the creation of, or usurp people's versions of, heaven or hell. Thus, led by religion, people may end up in the religion's idea of heaven, which to them may be far from optimal. For instance religion and pregnancy may lead someone to marry and settle down where they're more suited to an outrageously dangerous lifestyle with nobody left to grieve if they die.
1.1.21.3.2.1. Con: This is an Abraham-centric generalization of "religion."  Taoism, Confucianism, Hinduism, and Buddhism provide frameworks for a person to understand their relationship with their self, the people around them, and the world around them, and the purpose of these relationships. An argument about the utility of religion cannot simply cast aside half of the world's religious history as if it is irrelevant.
1.1.21.4. Pro: Religions have successfully provided imagery of tales and protagonists, and associated that to models for sensitivity, understanding, thought, action, and interaction, which can be applied both on individual and social levels, and to people of different upbringings.
1.1.21.4.1. Con: The same has been done by literature, without giving massive power to the writers.
1.1.21.4.2. Con: Many of the "protagonists" in religious tales are negative role models if emulated. For example, in the judeo-christian story of Abraham, he is willing to kill his son for religious purposes. Later he kills an animal for religious purposes. This character is widely believed to be "good" by followers of judeo-christian religions.
1.1.21.5. Con: Religion tells people to be kind and compassionate to others lest they fall from grace. Humans should be kind to each other because it's the right thing to do, not for fear of a gods wrath and judgment.
1.1.22. Con: Religious texts are infinitely fallible because they are man-made products of whimsy, poetry, mythology and some history woven together into a new whole.
1.1.22.1. Con: If religion is man-made, then all man-made philosophies would be equally as fallible.
1.1.22.1.1. Con: The difference between religion and other philosophies are that religion is typically un-falsifiable while things like science and math can be used and tested and be shown to be legitimate and shown to work.
1.1.23. Con: Religion did not invent "moral codes" it implemented them.
1.1.23.1. Pro: Basic morality is an evolutionary adaptation, that may be traced back to the need of our ancestors to survive in small groups in Savannah and ultimately to [the selfish gene theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene-centered_view_of_evolution#Selfish-gene_theory).
1.1.23.1.1. Pro: Some aspects of morallity are observed even in non-human animals, e.g. [bonobo and chimpanzees](http://www.earthisland.org/journal/index.php/elist/eListRead/chimps_and_bonobos_prove_that_moral_behavior_is_a_product_of_evolution/).
1.1.23.2. Pro: The predisposition toward caring has been [observed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_learning_in_animals) in a wide variety of animals. Neurophilosophy and [neurosciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience) in general tend to show that morality as we know it, might be a survival tool given by evolution processes. The better a species get as using this tool, the better it will perform in an evolutionary context.
1.1.24. Con: Religious moral claim usually looks like a blackmail tactic. People should follow tenets or be condemned and punished in the afterlife.
1.1.24.1. Con: Religions provide a different incentive. People may choose not to punch others because they might get thrown in prison. That is another form of blackmail. If all people's actions were perfect, there would never need to be incentives to behave, but we seem to need them.
1.1.24.1.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.
1.2. Pro: Religions emerged as an evolutionary adaptation. They spread the adoption of behaviors that provided evolutionary advantages.
1.2.1. Con: Religion has also spread behaviors that provide evolutionary disadvantages.
1.2.1.1. Pro: Martyrdom has long been celebrated by religions and can in some cases encourage disastrous behaviors such as suicide bombing.
1.2.1.2. Pro: Many religions over time have engaged in human sacrifice.
1.2.1.2.1. Con: Human sacrifice could have had [evolutionary benefits](http://www.sciencemag.org/news/2016/04/human-sacrifice-may-have-helped-societies-become-more-complex). Thus the prevalence of human sacrifice does not necessarily counteract the evolutionary benefit of religion.
1.2.1.3. Pro: Religion may have spread traits such as gullibility, cowardice or conformity.
1.2.1.3.1. Pro: Education tends to reduce human proclivity to [gullibility](https://theconversation.com/why-are-some-people-more-gullible-than-others-72412) and, at the same time, those more educated tend to be less religious.
1.2.1.3.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.1.
1.2.1.3.2. Pro: According to research, religious people tend to have specific traits that remain constant cross-culturally and cross-religiously: religiosity is associated with to high [agreeableness](https://cdn.uclouvain.be/public/Exports%20reddot/psyreli/documents/2003.EOLSS.pdf) and conscientiousness.
1.2.1.3.2.1. Pro: In terms of [values](https://cdn.uclouvain.be/public/Exports%20reddot/psyreli/documents/2003.EOLSS.pdf), religious individuals \(regardless of particular faith or culture\) tend to give higher importance to "tradition, conformity, and benevolence", and low  importance to "hedonism, stimulation, and   self-direction".
1.2.1.3.3. Pro: Religion often relies on simple and intuitive cognitive processes, rather than complex ones.
1.2.1.3.3.1. Pro: [Cognitive fluency](https://www.uxmatters.com/mt/archives/2011/07/how-cognitive-fluency-affects-decision-making.php),  a “subjective experience of the ease or difficulty of completing a mental task”, also makes people believe things or like them because those things feel familiar, are well-expressed and in tune with their own expectations. This could explain why self-assuring religious [myths](http://www.bbc.com/future/story/20160323-why-are-people-so-incredibly-gullible) are easier to believe regardless of factual information.
1.2.1.3.3.2. Pro: Human cognitive process tend to rely on intuition rather than [analysis](http://www.bbc.com/future/story/20160323-why-are-people-so-incredibly-gullible) to save energy. Therefore, if ideas come from familiar sources, other people believe them and align with our own beliefs and are good in terms of storytelling, we may tend believe them, even if proper scrutiny would render them false.
1.2.1.3.3.2.1. Pro: Humans have evolved to deal with [information](https://theconversation.com/why-are-some-people-more-gullible-than-others-72412) in two different ways: in a fast, automatic and intuitive process and in a slow, analytical and rational way. As we tend to have a positivity bias \(we assume people act honestly\) and a confirmation bias \(we tend to believe what fits our views\), the first way is often used and while good in ancestral small groups, it can also be dangerous, especially in bigger and more developed societies.
1.2.1.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.6.2.1.3.
1.2.1.5. Con: Religions that majorly spread evolutionary disadvantageous behaviors either went extinct, have been assimilated or are regarded as primitive.
1.2.1.5.1. Con: Declaring religious practices primitive now does not lessen their negative impact on history.
1.2.1.5.2. Pro: When [Mayas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sacrifice_in_Maya_culture) encountered an environmental constraint \(drought\), their preferred solution was to reduce their population by sacrificing their peers to the rain god.
1.2.1.6. Pro: Being content with suffering and death in the hopes of an afterlife may cause some to resign to defeat.
1.2.1.7. Pro: Religions state that it is God who provides shelter, food, water, etc. This disconnects us from nature, which is "who" actually provide our resources.
1.2.1.8. Con: Just because an adaptation has negative byproducts does not make the adaptation as a whole maladaptive.
1.2.1.9. Con: The fact that we're still here kinda contradicts this argument. We're the survivors of humans with religion. Religion has been an evolutionary disadvantage mainly for those that were killed by people with religion, but not for us, the survivors.
1.2.1.10. Con: Disadvantages seen today may have been useful at some point in evolution, but are now considered [evolution remnants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_vestigiality).
1.2.1.11. Pro: Extreme pacifism promoted by faiths like [Janism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jainism#Non-violence_\(ahimsa\)), or [Anabaptist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anabaptism), among others, can make believers not able to defend themselves or others.
1.2.1.11.1. Con: Unwillingness to defend ones self is a personal choice that ought to be respected. Such a choice has no bearing on a persons ability to defend ones self.
1.2.1.11.1.1. Con: If someone is born and indoctrinated into a culture or religion which promotes absolute pacifism it is more a product of that than of their own personal informed choice.
1.2.1.11.2. Con: Jehovah's Witnesses have never worried about defending themselves with arms. Their more effective [defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_cases_involving_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_by_country) has been in the courts.
1.2.1.11.3. Con: Others may protect them but they won't defend others. This seems to create inequity.
1.2.1.11.3.1. Con: Protection should be provided to them by dedicated law enforcement officers. They are not obliged to take that role.
1.2.1.11.4. Con: Violence only begets more violence. Hence, the act of not resorting to violence is good for humanity, not bad. Violence is not the only route to protecting one's self.
1.2.1.11.4.1. Con: Many progressive movements have only gained influence through the use of violence. Even passive resistance demands violence against self in order to succeed.
1.2.1.11.4.2. Con: Sometimes a word or action is so abhorrent that a non-violent response would not be enough. Ignoring , turning the other cheek or responding with more words could be an act of tolerance, and we should not tolerate the intolerant.
1.2.1.11.4.3. Pro: All violence can be seen to be the result of words failing. So long as there is a chance for humans to discuss things and continue a dialogue, will not feel the need to resort to violence. If violence has occurred, it follows that we have either not used language correctly \(or at all\) or that our argument has failed. Sometimes our argument is successful and the other cannot find an argument to resist, and at this point they may respond with violence. Violence stems from a lack of words.
1.2.1.11.4.3.1. Con: Some violence has nothing to do with communication or lack thereof.
1.2.1.11.4.3.1.1. Pro: For instance rape. It's frequently about power.
1.2.1.11.4.3.1.2. Pro: Abuse against spouses or children which is caused by anger issues and often aggravated by addiction is violence that asserts power and dominance but is not caused by lack of communication.
1.2.1.11.4.3.1.3. Pro: Violence related to [sadistic personality disorder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sadistic_personality_disorder) is caused by a condition in which someone derives pleasure on inflicting pain on others \(or oneself\).
1.2.1.11.4.4. Con: In some cases violence is the only reasonable response to violence. In the cases of mass genocide to not fight back would be to condemn millions to death.
1.2.1.11.4.4.1. Con: Martyrs who respond violence with non-violence often venerated. They are not seen as bad or evil. They were good and lived peacefully in accordance to universal moral authority even to the point of death.
1.2.1.11.4.4.1.1. Con: It is likely that many victims of genocide would rather have survived than be venerated.
1.2.1.11.4.5. Con: Being able to defend yourself does not imply voluntarily creating violence. Self-defence and malevolence are two distinct ideas.
1.2.1.11.4.6. Pro: Violence is not the only route. Seeking help from a stronger ally through use of diplomacy to intimidate your foe through the threat of possible violence is a way as well.
1.2.1.11.4.6.1. Con: Diplomacy was tried and failed in the case of Nazi Germany. Not only were the Nazis murdering German citizens but they were invading other countries, war was the only way to stop them.
1.2.1.11.4.6.2. Con: To be in a position to offer realistic threats of violence, you must have experience with self-defence so that it may be credible to your opponent.
1.2.1.11.4.7. Pro: Diplomacy and trade are options to deter violence so that you could protect yourself.
1.2.1.11.4.7.1. Con: -> See 1.2.1.11.4.6.1.
1.2.2. Con: Even a good evolutionary adaption can lead to evil and vice versa. Being natural doesn't mean it's good \(naturalistic fallacy\).
1.2.3. Con: Religion may have been a self-selecting cultural trait, which means that it has persisted without necessarily granting an evolutionary advantage.
1.2.3.1. Pro: Natural selection may in fact act on religious ideas, for example tales that are easier to remember may outcompete tales that are more challenging. This leads to some ideas spreading with no requirement for those ideas to provide their "host" individuals with an advantage \(this is part of the [meme hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_psychology_of_religion#Memes)\).
1.2.3.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.3.3.
1.2.3.1.2. Con: That a story is easier to remember may give it evolutionary value. The ability to quickly recall the 'moral' of a story can have application in practical ethics.
1.2.3.1.2.1. Con: The practical application depends on whether the morals of the story are actually beneficial themselves. Over time society is becoming more secular and discarding many of the morals of religion meaning society deems those morals as not beneficial.
1.2.3.2. Con: There is less evidence for a self-selecting mechanism than for one of genuine adaptation. For example, [surveys](https://www.edge.org/conversation/jonathan_haidt-moral-psychology-and-the-misunderstanding-of-religion) have shown that "religious [believers](http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-2886974/Study-Religious-people-happier-life-satisfaction-others.html) in the United States are [happier](https://theconversation.com/are-religious-people-happier-than-non-religious-people-87394), healthier, [longer-lived](https://edition.cnn.com/2016/05/16/health/religion-lifespan-health/index.html), and more generous to charity and to each other than are secular people."
1.2.3.2.1. Con: Suveys don't provide reliable information about evolutionary advantage.
1.2.4. Con: It seems unlikely that evolution created religion. Thousands of people didn't wake up one morning with the same set of unfounded assumptions and decide to write them down and start praying to them.
1.2.4.1. Pro: Most religions have an account for the creation of the religion, an account that occurs before it became widespread.
1.2.5. Pro: Religion provides a solution in the face of nihilism and the dramatic nature of existence. This is called the [Terror management theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terror_management_theory).
1.2.5.1. Con: There are other ways to find meaning in life besides religion, such as through living for others by helping them, or attaching value to material goods such as money or wealth. Religion is not the only way to beat back nihlism
1.2.5.1.1. Con: Altruism is most commonly found in religious traditions, while too much wealth causes anxiety and is therefore not a good option for beating back nihilism. Religion is foundationally about finding meaning and is therefore the oldest and arguably best way to find meaning in ones life.
1.2.5.1.1.1. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.1.3.6.
1.2.5.2. Con: Religion does not solve the problem of nihlism, because it never justifies why life has value; it claims that it does because of God. Thus, it would not satisfy a nihlist who was looking for some reason why life had value, since the religious justification depends on an unproven notion of God and his or her actions.
1.2.6. Con: Religion could also be a by-product of the evolutionary development of consciousness. For example, it could represent a [search of meaning where there is none](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_detection).
1.2.6.1. Con: Thinking that there is a meaning in something helps us to restore feelings of certainty and clarity which in turn could improve our [self-esteem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-esteem). Thus, it could be considered as a useful evolutionary adaptation.
1.2.6.2. Con: Religion was likely an unexpected [spin-off](https://www.newscientist.com/article/mg23631561-000-effortless-thinking-the-godshaped-hole-in-your-brain/) of a useful adaptation - empahty. The need to understand the motives of the group members, crucial for survival, was re-employed to explain non-human objects' behavior. This good adaptation leads first to animism and ultimately to religion.
1.2.6.2.1. Con: Despite the religion being a possible spin-off of a positive adaptation - empathy - it does not justify the religion as something necessarily positive. Just as the ability to store fat was positive for hunter-gathers, but became a major cause of death due to obesity in the modern society, religion becomes one of the major causes for unnecessary violence and anti-scientific thinking.
1.2.6.2.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.1.1.
1.2.6.3. Con: If religion was just a by-product of human's characteristics, it would not have become the dominant organizing system of every society on earth. This demonstrates that it was a [useful adaptation](http://assets.press.princeton.edu/chapters/s10063.pdf), and not a maladaption \(at least at the time\).
1.2.6.3.1. Pro: Despite predictions of religions' demise in the last centuries, most humans in the world are still religious and religions have been growing and mutating at a quick pace \([Norenzayan, p. 2\)](http://assets.press.princeton.edu/chapters/s10063.pdf).
1.2.6.3.1.1. Pro: Estimates calculate that there are about 10,000 religions in the world, with most people adhering to a low number of big religions. Worldly, there are 2 billions of self-identified Christians and 1.3 people identify as Muslims \([Norenzayan, p.2](http://assets.press.princeton.edu/chapters/s10063.pdf)\).
1.2.6.3.1.2. Con: In Australia, religiously [unaffiliated](http://www.abs.gov.au/ausstats/abs\@.nsf/Lookup/by+Subject/2071.0~2016~Main+Features~Religion+Data+Summary~70) people have increased from less than 1% in 1966, to over 30% in 2016.
1.2.6.3.1.2.1. Con: This only applies to Australia, not the world.
1.2.6.3.1.3. Con: In Europe, the number of non-religious citizens, especially among young adults, is [increasing](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/mar/21/christianity-non-christian-europe-young-people-survey-religion).
1.2.6.3.1.4. Con: There is only one religion whose percentage share of the [population is expected to grow](http://www.pewforum.org/2015/04/02/religious-projections-2010-2050/) and that is Islam. This is only because [Muslims have the highest fertility rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_population_growth) of any religious group and is far above the average rate of the world population.
1.2.6.3.2. Con: While some religion may have thrived and survived as they provided advantages \(social cohesion, cooperation, rules\), some present-day societies are successful at “sustaining large-scale cooperation with institutions such as court, police and mechanisms for enforcing contracts” \([Norenzayan, p.9](http://assets.press.princeton.edu/chapters/s10063.pdf)\).
1.2.6.3.2.1. Pro: In Scandinavian countries, strong institutions that facilitate cooperation “usurped” the community-building functions of religion, creating societies that are “some of the most cooperative, peaceful, and prosperous in the world” and thus making religion useless [\(Norenzayan, p.9\)](http://assets.press.princeton.edu/chapters/s10063.pdf).
1.2.6.3.2.2. Con: The fact that other systems can, through reason or otherwise, replace religion, doesn't mean that religion hasn't been, up until then, the dominant and successful adaptation.
1.2.6.3.2.3. Con: The long-term effects of such replacements are not clear and there are examples of dismantling religion in communist countries which, at least partially, led to undesireable long-term consequences.
1.2.6.3.2.3.1. Con: The quoted [study](http://assets.press.princeton.edu/chapters/s10063.pdf) does not talk about countries or systems that tried to dismantle or antagonize religion, but democratic countries with freedom of religion that provide a system, alongside religion, that offers much of the same benefits.
1.2.6.3.2.3.1.1. Pro: In that scenario of secular and religious competition, most developed countries tend to become less religious.
1.2.6.3.2.3.1.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.
1.2.6.3.2.3.1.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.2.1.1.
1.2.6.3.2.3.1.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.3.1.1.13.3.2.3.5.1.1.1.1.3.
1.2.6.3.3. Pro: Researchers consider that prosocial religions proliferated through “cultural diffusion, population expansions, and conquest” as they managed to forge “anonymous strangers into large, cohesive moral communities tied together with the sacred bonds of a common supernatural jurisdiction” \([Norenzayan, p. 9](http://assets.press.princeton.edu/chapters/s10063.pdf)\).
1.2.6.4. Pro: Religion has been helpful in leading us to science as a means to understand the world around us. At any given point in time religion has filled in the gaps of knowledge we have, leading us to innovation that brightens those dark spots. As we build the means to see and understand those gaps, science takes over, but religious belief allowed us to survive and evolve enough to replace superstition with demonstrable truth.
1.2.6.4.1. Con: Religions historically have claimed to already know the answers to questions science asks. Filling in the gaps with unsupported claims does not encourage inquiry because it thinks it already has the answers.
1.2.6.4.1.1. Pro: Many people who dared to defy given answers were [burnt as heretics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_people_burned_as_heretics).
1.2.6.4.1.2. Pro: The big religions are based on revelation, not exploration. If one believes that the most important information in the world already has been written, it tends to cause less curiosity about science and the world as we see it today.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1. Pro: Belief is unfounded assumption. Assume one false thing and any false thing can be proved true. Thus it undermines our rationality.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1. Con: Much of what we use to navigate the world is based on unfounded assumptions, belief is in no way unique.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.1. Pro: People may choose certain foods because they think they are healthier without going through the process of verifying it.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.1.1. Con: It is very easy to verify whether a food is healthy or not by looking at the nutritional information. That people do not do so is bad.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.2. Pro: People assume a certain street or route may be less dangerous or assume someone may intend harm and avoid that person or place, even if those beliefs are not founded or verified.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.3. Pro: People are willing to believe that a politician will bring jobs and vote for him or her, even if they have not verified it.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.3.1. Con: Believing that a politician will bring jobs is typically a verifiable claim and that people do not verify it is indeed a bad thing.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.3.1.1. Con: Not every politician has a history that shows success or failure at creating jobs.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.3.3.2.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.5. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.3.3.1.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6. Con: The fact that it is difficult to live without making unfounded assumptions doesn't mean that any particular unfounded assumption is a good thing.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1. Pro: Unfounded assumptions come with varying degrees of unfoundedness and consequence. The higher the unfoundedness and the consequence the less sound is the assumption.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1. Pro: Religions often present what appears to be a lot of foundation, an entire book and other items. However they usually also request a lot of unfounded assumptions and the consequences of making the unfounded assumptions are often substantial.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.1. Con: The foundation presented can be the result of centuries of cherry picking the most consistent passages from supporters while destroying opposing/inconsistent views and/or killing or imprisoning or ostracizing the inconvenient authors. Thus even those facts that can be verified can be considered to amount to anecdotal evidence at best.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2. Pro: Most religions use the you-have-nothing-to-lose-by-believing argument. Of course you do: There's your time, your independence, your objectivity, and your cash.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.1. Pro: If one is believing in religion purely because they have nothing to lose or to hedge bets then it is not a genuine belief and one loses their intellectual integrity. At the same time an omniscient deity would surely know that the belief is not genuine.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2. Pro: Much time is spent praying. Though many say their prayers are answered, evidence of a causal link between their prayers and the outcome that occurred is lacking.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.1. Pro: [Studies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Studies_on_intercessory_prayer) have shown prayer has no effect beyond placebo.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.1.1. Pro: It's worse than that you've also wasted your time.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2. Con: Praying may have consequences on [brain](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/10/18/how-does-prayer-meditation-affect-brain-activity_n_1974621.html) activity, function and structure.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.1. Pro: Prayer shows a specific pattern in [brain activity](https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=104310443), lighting frontal lobes \(that affect concentration\) while parietal lobes go dark. This last area is responsible for sensory experiences and could explain that those praying “lose their sense of self, feel a sense of oneness, a blurring of the boundary between self and other”.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.1.1. Pro: Those [results](https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=104310443) were consistent with different religious practitioners, from Franciscan nuns praying to Buddhists meditating or Sikhs chanting.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.1.2. Con: These results would have been found when the subjects knew that they and their brain activity were being observed. So these results are as \(or less\) normal as behavior on reality TV shows.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.2. Pro: [Research](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2944261/) with Buddhist monks suggests that "over the course of meditating for tens of thousands of hours, the long-term practitioners had actually altered the structure and function of their brains".
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.2.1. Con: The average religious believer and practitioner may not have the same commitment, tools and training as Buddhist monks to be able to achieve such results.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.2.1.1. Con: Any form or degree of [positive thinking](https://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/stress-management/in-depth/positive-thinking/art-20043950) or [meditation](https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=104310443) is beneficial for the human mind.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.3. Con: [Neuroplasticity](https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=104310443), the capacity of our brains to change and adapt, is not a unique characteristic of religion but of extreme concentration and 'mental trainning'.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.2.2.3.1. Pro: The more someone can [focus](https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=104310443) on something "math or auto racing or football or God", the more that becomes their own reality, as it  "becomes written into the neural connections of your brain", experts say.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.3. Pro: Much social power, over the religious and/or to speak or act on their behalf, is ceded to religious leaders.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.4. Pro: Once you make unfounded assumptions that are relevant to your decisions/opinions your ability to make those decisions or draw conclusions objectively is at risk.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5. Pro: Some part of donations to the church may result in charitable work that the giver would otherwise make through different means. However, the efficiency will suffer from [overheads](https://galileounchained.com/2012/05/14/are-churches-more-like-charities-or-country-clubs/): for instance the livelihood of a preacher and his boss, and his boss's boss etc, and the buildings they work and live in, their private jets, the adverts, pomp, and the expensive art that adorns their window-frames, walls, ceilings or vaults, and legal fees.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5.1. Pro: Many religious institutions exist mainly for financial gain, and some are corrupt.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5.1.1. Pro: Most of the world’s [biggest landowners](http://www.businessinsider.com/worlds-biggest-landowners-2011-3) are monarchs from countries with official state religions that support the monarchy or heads of religions themselves.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5.1.1.1. 1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5.1.1.2. 1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5.1.1.4. Pro: [Queen Elizabeth II](http://www.businessinsider.com/worlds-biggest-landowners-2011-3#2-king-abdullah-of-saudi-arabia-14), UK’s monarch and Head of State, is considered to be the biggest landowner of the world.

1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5.1.3. 1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.2.5.1.3.1. Pro: As a result of the prosperity gospel many [megachurch](http://dustoffthebible.com/Blog-archive/2015/10/28/15-religious-leaders-that-make-more-money-getting-out-of-bed-than-youll-make-all-year/) [leaders](https://www.cnn.com/2015/03/13/living/creflo-dollar-jet-feat/index.html) have their own private jets and exorbitant amounts of money while their congregations remain impoverished or at average income.
1.2.6.4.1.2.1.1.6.1.1.3. Pro: A lot of the foundation is often unfounded itself, frequently based on other unfounded assumptions in a web that can be difficult to unravel, thus disguising the ultimate unfoundedness of much of it.
1.2.6.4.2. Con: There is no evidence to suggest that those gaps being filled with place holders and superstitions was necessary for our survival and evolution.
1.2.6.4.3. Con: Heads of religions recognize only the parts of science which fit the description of the world they already give to the masses. All other science is called "sacrilege" and "untrue" and the proponents are persecuted. That narrows fields of scientific research and slows down the spread of new discoveries. Examples: [Book burning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book_burning#Christian_burnings), [Galileo Galilei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei), [Charles Darwin](http://www.bbc.co.uk/science/0/22078983).

1.2.7. Con: The evolutionary advantage may have been that if you went along with the dominant religion you would not be murdered by the dominant religion.
1.2.8. Pro: Religion was probably indispensable for most of human history in that it [improved the strength](https://www.wikiwand.com/en/Evolutionary_psychology_of_religion#/Religion_as_an_adaptation) of small groups to outcompete other groups.
1.2.8.1. Con: This is classic "others must fail" thinking. How would a religious group outperform the non-religious? By ostracizing or killing them or forcing them to comply. The fact that there was a victor does not mean that overall efficiency was raised.
1.2.8.1.1. Con: Before the advent of modern ethics, a religious group had a significant advantage on the level of moral compliance of its members \(because of divine omniscience\), thus outperforming in the overall cooperation.
1.2.8.2. Con: Competition is a good thing where it leads to progress, but religions do not change so when a religious group wins progress is less likely.
1.2.8.2.1. Con: Religions are constantly changing. The rate of change is slow, but that is a positive because it forces new ideas to be tested sufficiently before the new ideas are accepted.
1.2.8.2.1.1. Con: Religion is dogmatic in nature since it believes it is divinely inspired. As such the changes it makes is when it acquiesces to secular moral pressure and the large amount of time this takes prolongs oppression.

Without beliefs in omniscient judges of morality, it may have never been applied.

1.2.9. Pro: Much of the practices of religion are conducive towards good mental health. It is therefore likely that religion has been a good mediator of mental health for humans.

Masturbation was the most frequent sexual activity, followed by affairs with women, sex with male companions, and Internet pornography.

1.2.9.7.1.5. 1.2.9.7.1.6. Con: John Jay researchers reported that about 4 % of the 110,000 priests studied had been accused of sexual misconduct involving children. There is no consensus about the sexual abuse among the general American male population, but estimates are 1 in 10 men or close to 5% and thus [the rate of abuse by Catholic priests is not higher](http://www.newsweek.com/priests-commit-no-more-abuse-other-males-70625) than the national estimates.
1.2.9.7.1.6.1. Con: The study was "[authorized and is being paid for by the U.S. Conference of Catholic Bishops](http://www.newsweek.com/priests-commit-no-more-abuse-other-males-70625)".

1.2.9.7.2.1. Pro: A US Marriage Survey conducted in 2011 recorded responses from girls involved in child marriages from Hindu, Buddhist, Catholic, Baptist, Muslim, and other [faiths](https://www.teenvogue.com/story/child-marriage-and-religion-in-the-united-states).

1.2.9.7.2.2.1. Con: However, among sects who force generally young girls to marry older men, [religious reasons](https://www.teenvogue.com/story/child-marriage-and-religion-in-the-united-states) are used to coerce the children.

1.2.9.7.2.4.1. 1.2.9.8.2.1. Con: While 72% of Americans say to believe in Heaven, 58% of adults also believe in Hell, which makes for a large number of people who can fear that sins in this life will condemn them in the afterlife.

1.2.10. Pro: Religion led people to do things correctly before science and technology caught up.

1.2.10.2. Pro: Before modern states could provide welfare, religion was the only source of education, healthcare or economic relief.
1.2.10.2.1. Pro: Hospitals were founded, financed, and staffed by religions. An old [French term](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_hospitals) for hospital is hôtel-Dieu, "hostel of God."
1.2.10.2.2. Pro: Religious organizations build schools \(and universities\), orphanages, and other services for community benefits.

1.2.10.2.5. Pro: Judaic religious tradition has throughout history [emphasised education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_education) which has been an advantage to its adherents at places and times where illiteracy was the norm, for example in [Europe in the early middle ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literacy#Ancient_and_post-classical_literacy).
1.2.10.2.5.1. Con: Judaic education in reading was historically reserved for boys.
1.2.10.2.6. Pro: The Catholic Church was the only institution in Europe during several hundred years that actively contributed to free education for the masses.
1.2.10.2.6.1. Pro: The Church also mandated in 1179 [free education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_education#Education_in_ancient_civilization) for the poor, so every cathedral had a master to teach boys too poor to pay the regular fee, planting the seed of modern universal and public education.
1.2.10.3. Con: Religion also taught people to do many things wrong. Such as exorcism for mental illness, human sacrifice to appease gods, and relying on faith healing instead of medicine.
1.2.10.3.1. Con: Faith healing can be viewed as producing a [placebo effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Placebo).
1.2.10.3.1.1. Con: Since Placebo effects typically do not fix the underlying condition and only act as a bandage for the problem this is not necessarily a good thing.
1.2.10.3.2. Con: Rituals can have a [Causal impact](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/why-rituals-work/) on people’s thoughts, feelings, and behaviors.
1.2.10.3.3. Pro: Amputating a working body part, the male [foreskin](http://www.bbc.co.uk/ethics/malecircumcision/religions_1.shtml), is an excellent example of something wrong being forced and enforced by religion.
1.2.10.4. Con: Religion just fills the holes and gaps until science discovers the answers and as such stifled inquiry.
1.2.10.5. Con: Arguing that religions have done some good is easy but almost everything leads to some amount of good. It is more useful to argue that religion has caused a net amount of good but doing this calculation is very hard and thus it is almost impossible to conclusively show that religion has been a good thing overall.
1.2.10.6. Con: These "correct things" can easily be derived from observation and do not require a system of religious belief to be enforced.
1.2.10.6.1. Pro: Religion occupies advancements as if it was the sole inventor even after centuries of resistance to them.
1.2.10.6.2. Con: Jewish dietary and hygiene laws had an entire people group treating germs and bacteria correctly for many thousands of years before germs and bacteria were discovered \(which famously led them to be remarkably unaffected by the Black Plague among other things\).
1.2.10.6.2.1. Con: Although some religions helped to disseminate hygiene rules, this was not always true. The Roman practice of public baths [was seen as 'sinful' by early christians](https://pdxscholar.library.pdx.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?referer=https://www.google.com/&httpsredir=1&article=1126&context=younghistorians), who abhorred nudity and went on a crusade against what was seen as a pagan luxury. The condemnation was not unanimous, but it was prevailing.

In such a non-plural  environment, it would be a fallacy to say that "Religion led people to act correctly..." because there was no testable alternative to see if a non-religious life was "more correct" or "less correct" than a religious lifestyle.

Rituals are a cornerstone of human conduct and help bind together a society.

The [Greek civilisation](https://education.onehowto.com/article/the-origin-of-philosophy-the-transition-from-myth-to-logos-2313.html) starts explaining the world through religious myths, until philosophers consider it necessary to find a more rational explanation \(logos\) starting a strong tradition of Western rationalism.
1.2.13.2.1. Con: Recent [scholars](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s40647-016-0144-9) point that the [transition](https://www.jstor.org/stable/41722132?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents) from 'myth' to 'logos' was a continuum, so rational and mythical explanations were never in conflict.
1.2.13.2.1.1. Pro: Having a global understanding of the universe, although possibly filled by irrational beliefs, is an important part of our psyche. It uses intuition and pattern recognition to make decisions and solve problems. The other process thinks rationally, limits the context to what is already known to work and can be articulated precisely.

Although there is some debate on the [lateralization of those processes](http://ssh://git\@git.sarbakan.com:10023/mobility-ware/destination-solitaire/solitaire-customer-tool-frontend.git), [both are important part of your brains mechanisms](https://youtu.be/OxslBI3hNFQ?t=2943) and are in no way mutually exclusive.

1.2.13.2.3.4.1. Con: Societies organised around religious values provide a stable framework for their citizens to be safe and comfortable enough in order to contemplate their own thinking, which can then lead to innovations.
