There is no evidence for a key role of religious values in these societies; basic human needs and the objective benefits of cooperation can account for these innovations.
1.2.13.3. Pro: Religions are both good and bad.  They form part of the evolution of modern society towards greater humanity and a growing awareness of our individual vulnerability and interdependence. This period of human development, while incomplete, is slowly coming to an end as religious belief declines.
1.2.13.4. Pro: Regrouping behind common archetypal [ideals](http://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/2153599X.2015.1063001?journalCode=rrbb20) increases coordination, cooperation and chances for survival and reproduction.
1.2.13.4.1. Con: Religion fragments the commonality of each state and other organisations to those who are of the religion and those who are not, thus reducing coordination and cooperation. For instance there are multiple examples of religious groups not cooperating with local law enforcement or defying local law, which has been known to result in loss of life or liberty.

1.4.9.1.1. Con: Much of the West has its own system of separating people. While not as explicitly as cast, class divides can still divide people for their [entire life](https://www.theatlantic.com/business/archive/2016/07/social-mobility-america/491240/), [prevent marriages](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/02/23/upshot/rise-in-marriages-of-equals-and-in-division-by-class.html), and trap people for [generations](https://www.economist.com/blogs/graphicdetail/2015/03/daily-chart-11).

1.4.9.1.1.2. Con: The [East](https://blogs.adb.org/blog/responding-income-inequality-asia), including [India](https://www.hindustantimes.com/india-news/rich-poor-divide-in-india-widening-as-economy-grows-report/story-5iyHD5PbJa4kqCw8qBrNsO.html), also has [divisions](https://apjjf.org/-Yoshio-Sugimoto/3419/article.html) among classes for [economic](http://www.straitstimes.com/singapore/new-study-finds-class-divide-in-singapore) reasons, aside from \(and often intertwined with\) religious-based divisions such as castes.
1.4.9.2. Pro: [Sikhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism#Justice_and_equality) advocates for a God without form or gender. Everyone is [equal](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/sikhism/beliefs/beliefs.shtml) in front of God and has equal direct access to God. Sikhism also commands believers to use ordinary life to be closer to God, to strive for social justice and to live honestly.
1.4.9.2.1. Pro: The Sikh code of conduct does not deal with [abortion](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/sikhism/sikhethics/abortion.shtml), or many other bioethical issues, and the practice is not uncommon among the Sikh community in India.
1.4.9.2.1.1. Con: Sikhism, from a theoretical perspective, still forbids [abortion](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/sikhism/sikhethics/abortion.shtml) and considers it a sin.
1.4.9.2.2. Pro: Sikhism considers men and women as [equals](http://www.wahegurunet.com/role-of-women-in-sikhism). Even if [gender discrimination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Sikhism) exists because it is roted in culture, in the Sikh society there is no religious basis for it.
1.4.9.2.2.1. Pro: In fact, in the 15th century, Sikhism was the first known major religion to advocate the equality of all people, especially [women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Sikhism).
1.4.9.2.3. Con: Although Sikhism has no specific teachings about [homosexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism_and_sexual_orientation), in modern times there is a divide between those who condemn it and those who consider it an acceptable option within Sikhism.

Pro: Buddhism, for example, does not provide strict and unanimous moral teachings on issues like [abortion](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/buddhism/buddhistethics/abortion.shtml), [death penalty](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/buddhism/buddhistethics/capitalpunishment.shtml) or [euthanasia](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/buddhism/buddhistethics/euthanasiasuicide.shtml).

1.4.9.4.1.1. Pro: For example, traditional Buddhism reject [abortion](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/buddhism/buddhistethics/abortion.shtml) and Buddhism is also against [contraceptive](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/buddhism/buddhistethics/contraception.shtml) methods used when the egg is fertilized. Although not explicitly, Buddha's teachings would be against the [death penalty](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/buddhism/buddhistethics/capitalpunishment.shtml) and regarding [euthanasia](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/buddhism/buddhistethics/euthanasiasuicide.shtml) the most common position is that it is wrong.

1.5.4. Pro: Islam has supported gender inequality.
1.5.4.1. Pro: Islam supports a complementary vision of men and women with "a separation of social functions" in where "woman's sphere of operation is the home" and "a man's corresponding sphere is the outside world" which certainly [limits women's experiences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Islam#Gender_roles) and freedom.
1.5.4.1.1. Pro: Traditional interpretations of Islam require a woman to have her [husband's permission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Islam#Gender_roles) to leave the house and take up employment.
1.5.4.1.2. Pro: In Islam, men have authority over women and some religious interpretations of the Qur'an consider that allows [domestic violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_and_domestic_violence) against women.
1.5.4.1.3. Pro: Many Islamic religious leaders consider women unfit to [lead](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_as_imams#Mixed-gender_congregations) mixed-gender congregations.
1.5.4.2. Pro: Islamic law discriminates between men and women.
1.5.4.2.1. Pro: In some Islamic countries, the testimony of women is given [less weightage](https://islamqa.info/en/1105) in a court of law as compared to a man's.
1.5.4.2.2. Pro: Muslim men [are allowed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polygyny_in_Islam) to practice polygyny and can have up to a total of four wives at one time. Polyandry, the practice of a woman having more than one husband, however, is not permitted.
1.5.4.2.3. Con: Islam promotes egalitarianism, which is expressed by guaranteeing women certain rights such as the right to life, to education, to conduct business, maintain property, and to keep their names \([Galloway, p. 32](https://nsuworks.nova.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1013&context=shss_dcar_etd)\).
1.5.4.2.3.1. Con: The guarantee of a small number of rights, which often fail to materialize for women in [islamic states](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/saudi-arabia-womens-rights-driving-ban-lifted-marriage-custody-bank-accounts-travel-medical-a7969551.html), do not mean that Islam is feminist as Islamic scripture entrenches and emboldens oppressive gender roles in other aspects of its scripture.
1.5.4.2.3.2. Con: The scriptural guarantees of rights to women in Islam are limited by their depiction of women only in the roles of wives, mothers and daughters. As a result, they often marginalize those who fall outside the traditional paradigms of women depicted within scriptural texts. [\(p.31\)](https://openaccess.leidenuniv.nl/bitstream/handle/1887/17220/ISIM_21_Islamic_Feminism_and_Gender_Equality.pdf)
1.5.4.2.4. Pro: A man is [allowed to](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interfaith_marriage_in_Islam) marry a woman from among the People of the Book \(Jews and Christians\), but a woman can only marry a muslim.
1.5.4.2.5. Pro: Women are given a [lesser share](https://www.al-islam.org/faith-and-reason-ayatullah-mahdi-hadavi-tehrani/question-32-difference-inheritance-women-and-men) of inheritance as compared to men.
1.5.4.2.5.1. Con: This is a simplistic understanding of [Islamic law](http://www.dar-alifta.org/Foreign/ViewArticle.aspx?ID=4825&CategoryID=5). While a man does inherit twice what a women inherits, a man has a responsibility to provide for his female relations. This equals out the inheritance as the money a man inherits must be used in part to feed, shelter and clothe the women in his family, while all of the money the woman inherits she can keep without even the obligation to spend it on her own sustenance eg. food, clothing, medication.
1.5.4.2.5.1.1. Pro: A man has the complete [financial responsibility and duty](http://www.dar-alifta.org/Foreign/ViewFatwa.aspx?ID=8337) of running a household or a family. A woman has[no financial responsibility](http://womeninislam.ws/en/misconceptions_household-responsibilities.aspx) or obligation laid upon her by Shariah to provide for a household.
1.5.4.3. Pro: Under Islam recommended clothing is [more restrictive for women than men](http://www.abukhadeejah.com/understanding-the-muslim-dress-code-modesty-for-men-and-the-hijab-for-women-islam-4-5/).
1.5.5. Con: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.5.4.3.
1.5.6. Pro: Christianity has supported gender inequality.
1.5.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.15.1.4.
1.5.6.2. Pro: Christianity portrays a male deity, Father God, Son God, but no Mother God \(the virgin is not god she is merely a sanctified human\).  There are twelve male apostles, not one woman. Women are portrayed as either weeping mothers \(virgin mary\) or prostitutes \(magdalene\). The same can be said for Islam or Judaism, where God is portrayed as male and women are not allowed in the religious hierarchy.
1.5.6.3. Pro: Throughout history, the Catholic Church favored laws that opposed [women's suffrage](https://classroom.synonym.com/the-catholic-church-womens-suffrage-12085123.html).
1.5.6.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.15.1.4.2.
1.5.6.5. Con: The Church in Medieval times regulated [marriages](https://www.publicmedievalist.com/got-rape-and-middle-ages/) and tried to establish that there was consent from both parties.
1.5.6.5.1. Con: The Church also established the notion of '[conjugal debt](https://books.google.es/books?id=itG09FGBMwMC&lpg=PP1&vq=marital+rape+in+middle+ages&dq=marital+rape+in+middle+ages&pg=PA249&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q&f=false)' in which satisfying the sexual needs of the spouse was mandatory. While that was equally required for men and women, at a time when women were almost considered property and [discriminated](https://www.publicmedievalist.com/got-rape-and-middle-ages/) against, giving away body autonomy equated to allowing abuse and assault within marriages.
1.5.6.5.2. Con: One of the ways the church regulated marriage was [the phrase "and obey" in the marriage vow](https://www.chicagomarriage.com/does-the-bride-have-to-say-obey-in-her-wedding-vows/) for the woman.
1.5.6.6. Pro: The [bible](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Titus+2&version=NIV) also [tells](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=1+Peter+3&version=NIV) women to be submissive and subject to their husband. This patriarchal model is commonly considered to be harmful today.
1.5.6.7. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.2.1.3.2.5.2.
1.5.7. Con: The fact that most religions are patriarchal in nature doesnt mean that religion is, by definition, patriarchal.
1.5.8. Con: Not all religions are patriarchal.
1.5.8.1. Pro: Of the religions with the most followers in the world \(Hinduism, Buddhism, Judaism, Christianity, and Islam\) only the last three \(judeo-christian\) religions are distinctively patriarchal, the other two are centered around a belief of balance and equality between 'opposing' forces, do not have male-dominated structures and do not have 'laws' that are sexist or discriminatory against females and can therefore be considered as non-patriarchal.
1.5.8.1.1. Con: While the patriarchal nature may certainly differ, [Buddhism](https://berkleycenter.georgetown.edu/posts/can-women-become-leaders-in-the-buddhist-tradition) teachings are not exempt of gender inequality and misogyny.
1.5.8.1.1.1. Pro: Bernard Faure, scholar of Asian religions, asserts that "like most clerical discourses, Buddhism is indeed [relentlessly misogynist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Buddhism#Women's_Spiritual_Attainment), but as far as misogynist discourses go, it is one of the most flexible and open to multiplicity and contradiction".
1.5.8.1.1.2. Pro: Traditional [Buddhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Buddhism#Women's_Spiritual_Attainment) presents the classical [dichotomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madonna%E2%80%93whore_complex#In_popular_culture) of women only being seen as mothers or "lustful temptresses or as evil incarnate".
1.5.8.1.1.3. Pro: LGBT [individuals](https://qz.com/india/586192/theres-a-misogynist-aspect-of-buddhism-that-nobody-talks-about/) cannot traditionally be ordained as monks or nuns, reflecting very strict and discriminating gender norms.
1.5.8.1.1.4. Pro: In [monastic](https://qz.com/india/586192/theres-a-misogynist-aspect-of-buddhism-that-nobody-talks-about/) life, there are more [rules](https://www.thoughtco.com/buddhism-and-sexism-449757) for nuns \(bhikkunis\) than monks \(bhikkus\) "and while everyone has to control their desires, women have the additional burden of not 'arousing the desires of men'".
1.5.8.1.1.4.1. Pro: In traditional stories, [women](https://qz.com/india/586192/theres-a-misogynist-aspect-of-buddhism-that-nobody-talks-about/) are often depicted as just a source of temptation. And while monks are the embodiments of 'dhamma' \(the path of enlightenment\), lustful insatiable women are the embodiments of 'samsara' \(the cycle of death and rebirths\).
1.5.8.1.1.5. Pro: In some Buddhist narratives, [women](https://berkleycenter.georgetown.edu/posts/can-women-become-leaders-in-the-buddhist-tradition) cannot be leaders as they are unable to reach enlightenment, which is believed to be a limitation of their gender.
1.5.8.1.1.5.1. Pro: Women can only reach enlightenment f if they gain good karma and are [reborn](https://berkleycenter.georgetown.edu/posts/can-women-become-leaders-in-the-buddhist-tradition) as men.
1.5.8.1.1.5.2. Pro: Several major monastic lineages in Sri Lanka, areas of Southeast Asia, and Tibetan cultural areas deny female renunciants full [ordination](https://berkleycenter.georgetown.edu/posts/can-women-become-leaders-in-the-buddhist-tradition).
1.5.8.1.1.5.3. Con: It is not because 'some' people/streams claim a thing that it is inherently related to the believe system they are part of. Exceptions can be found on both sides but there is no consensus across buddhistic leaders so it cannot be viewed as proof for the entire ideology.
1.5.8.1.1.6. Con: [Recent research](https://vc.bridgew.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?referer=https://www.google.com/&httpsredir=1&article=1923&context=jiws) suggest that indeed Buddhist practices are not exempt from certain societal features \(of which gender discrimination is an element\) but the underlying ideology of buddhism supercedes 'worldly' things such as gender-identification by their innate search for 'egolessness' and related concepts.
1.5.8.1.2. Pro: There are no male leaders who directly infer their authority from a deity in [Hinduism](https://www.quora.com/Who-is-the-current-spiritual-leader-of-Hinduism#) or in [Buddhism](https://www.quora.com/Is-the-Dalai-Lama-like-the-Pope-of-Buddhism). The spiritual leaders are influential in their wide following but they are not considered as a figure of authority who can pass sentences, proclaims the 'truth' \(in the voice of a deity\) or is considered to be above-human. Islam, Christianity and Judaism do have only male authority figures who personify at least one of these elements.
1.5.8.1.2.1. Con: The fact that there are no male leaders who can set truths does not preclude Hinduism and Buddhism from promoting beliefs and practices that subjugate women and therefore contribute to a patriarchal system.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1. Pro: Although there is variance, there are many discriminatory and patriarchal teachings in [Hinduism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Hinduism) that limit women to be obedient daughters, housewives and mothers.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1. Con: The source explains there's 'also a strong Hindu tradition of questioning authority in order to deepen the understanding of these truths'. Meaning that although some scholars might interpret texts in a sexist way, the ideology itself doesn't have one \(male\) authority who can overrule everybody. The non-existence of a 'universal' truth in Hinduism is in fact supporting the claim that it is non-patriarchal \(compared to judeo-christian religions where this truth is claimed to be 'self-evident'\).
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1. Con: The fact that Hinduism does not have one male authority able to sanction absolute truth, in the same way that Judeo-Christian traditions do, does not mean several practices within Hinduism are not [patriarchal](https://www.nytimes.com/roomfordebate/2013/01/08/with-children-when-does-religion-go-too-far/in-hinduism-respect-the-sacred-ignore-the-sexism) since they place men at the top and women at the bottom.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: Many forms of [marriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Hinduism#Practices) in Hinduism include the father giving away his daughter without consent, therefore positioning women as the property of their fathers or husbands, which is certainly [patriarchal](http://damienmarieathope.com/2017/05/sexism-prejudice-and-killing-in-vedic-culture-hinduism/).
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.2. Pro: [Widowed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Hinduism#Practices) women are expected to pursue a spiritual life, in some cases being denied the possibility to remarry.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.3. Pro: While [Sati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Hinduism#Practices) is today an obsolete practice, traditionally, women would immolate themselves at their husband pyre or commit suicide. The opposite was not a established practice.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.3.1. Pro: Women killing themselves when their husbands die certainly makes their [worth](http://www.mahavidya.ca/2008/06/21/sati-and-social-implications/) related to their husbands and not themselves as human beings.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.3.2. Con: This does not specifically mean the religion is patriarchal as it can also be viewed as women having absolute power over life and death \(as carriers of life they also have the power to create death\). In Asian cultures this duality often leads to respect and reverence to females. It does however have very little to do with the 'worldly' practices of institutionalised \(patriarchal\) religion.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.3.2.1. Con: Sati is or was not about women having the power to control their lives, by that logic, suicide should be an option at any point. Women killed themselves only when their husbands died, which showed how their worth was completely tied to their husbands. Men did not commit suicide when their wives died.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.4. Con: Practices cannot be 'patriarchal' as patriarchy refers to an institution/structure based on power and authority. Practices can be discriminatory but discrimination does not imply patriarchal structures in itself.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.4.1. Con: [Patriarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patriarchy) refers to “a social system in which males hold primary power and predominate in roles of political leadership, moral authority, social privilege and control of property”. For that system to exist, social practices, even without a top-down formal authority, need to be indeed discriminatory towards women.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.4.2. Con: When wide discrimination towards women exist, and therefore there is a hierarchy between men and women, even if is not explicitly defined, that indeed in practice constitutes a patriarchal system.
1.5.8.1.2.1.1.1.1.5. Pro: [Gender equality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_inequality_in_India) in traditionally and present-day Hinduism [countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_inequality_in_Nepal) are among the [worst](https://www.usnews.com/news/best-countries/slideshows/the-10-worst-countries-for-gender-equality-ranked-by-perception?slide=8) of the [world](https://www.telegraph.co.uk/travel/maps-and-graphics/mapped-the-best-and-worst-countries-for-gender-equality/). When religion and culture are as intertwined as it is the case, the responsibility of religion in a patriarchal society cannot be denied.
1.5.8.1.2.1.2. Pro: Similar to judeo-christian traditions, Buddha's teachings also advise wives that to be "[obedient](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Buddhism#Women's_Spiritual_Attainment) to their husbands, please them, and not make them angry through their own desires".
1.5.8.1.2.1.2.1. Con: Buddha's teachings are only a small part of the entire religous body of knowledge and have been contested on several occassions, making it a disputed source that cannot be seen as the universal truth of the buddhist religion.
1.5.8.1.3. Pro: Contrary to judeo-christian traditions, there are [examples](https://www.thoughtco.com/buddhism-and-sexism-449757) of buddhist 'nuns' across Asia \(and more recently other parts of the world\) who are regarded in higher status than male monks or institutions where males and females are studying together. This can indicate that there is no inherent 'truth' of males being superior to females \(which is much more prominent in judeo-christian religions\).

But the overall image is far to complex to simply state that 'most of [them](http://www.beliefnet.com/columnists/religion101/2012/10/how-many-religions-are-there-part-five-the-hard-numbers.html)' are patriarchal.
1.5.8.2.1. Con: While it is true there are likely too many religions to determine what percentage is patriarchal [the majority of the human population is either Christian or Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_religious_populations) and thus most religious people fall into the category of belonging to a patriarchal religion.

If a parent was so controlling of they're child's behavior that they were incapable of ever doing anything wrong we'd at best call them a helicopter parent and at worst call them horribly abusive.
1.6.2.2.2.1.3.1. Con: Murdering people for no other reason than them being first born in their family is oppressive. Also an omnipotent god need not control peoples minds to free the Jews. If he can make food that tastes like whatever you want fall from the sky he can teleport the Jews out of Egypt without murdering any children.

1.6.2.2.4. Pro: [God orders the Israelites to exterminate](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Deuteronomy+7&version=NIV) all the existing tribes and peoples living in Israel.

Con: Although the biblical narrative commands the extermination of the of Canaanites, "mainstream Jewish traditions throughout history have treated these texts as [purely historical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism_and_warfare) or highly conditioned, and in either case not relevant to contemporary life".

1.6.2.2.9.1.1.1.1. The difference between these two stories being that it is the violence of the gods that leads them to cause the flood and it's God's desire to end violence that leads him to cause the flood.
1.6.2.2.9.1.1.1.2. Pro: In the story of [Noah](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Genesis+6&version=NIV), God loves Noah and so saves him. In the story of [Utnapishtim](http://www.ancienttexts.org/library/mesopotamian/gilgamesh/tab11.htm), the gods conspire to destroy men, but Ea rebels against the other gods as he often does.

The difference between these two stories is that in the story of Noah, the functioning of the universe \(God\) is of unified purpose to help Noah, while in the story of Utnapishtim the functioning of the universe \(gods\) is in chaos, and it is only by the work of trickery that Utnapishtim survives.
1.6.2.2.9.1.1.1.3. Pro: In the story of [Utnapishtim](http://www.ancienttexts.org/library/mesopotamian/gilgamesh/tab11.htm), Ea tells him to lie to the others who will not survive the flood while [God makes no such command to Noah](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Genesis+6&version=NIV).

Jewish Rabbis have argued that God actually [wanted Noah to argue on behalf of these other people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noah#Judaism).
1.6.2.2.9.1.1.1.4. Pro: The god of the earth Enlil is the instigator of the flood, who is angry when he learns that Ea has worked against him, suggesting that the earth has rejected man. When Noah is born it is prophesied that he will [comfort men regarding the curse](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Genesis+5&version=NIV) God has laid on the ground, and after the flood God states that [no longer will he curse the ground](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Genesis+8&version=NIV). Suggesting that the earth has accepted man in the story of Noah.
1.6.2.2.9.1.1.1.5. Pro: [Utnapishtim](http://www.ancienttexts.org/library/mesopotamian/gilgamesh/tab11.htm)'s effort in building the boat is painstakingly detailed. Noah's effort is outlined in a single [sentence](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Genesis+6%3A22&version=NIV).

The difference is that Utnapishtim survives by his hard work and the love of Ea while Noah survives by the love of God while a point is made elsewhere that Noah will give men rest from their work. Utnapishtim's work is valued while Noah's rest is valued.
1.6.2.2.9.1.1.1.6. Pro: In the story of Utnapishtim the gods end the flood because they are unhappy with what they have done while God ends the flood because he remembers Noah.

One story hinges on regret while the other story hinges on [remembering one's promises](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Genesis+8&version=NIV).
1.6.2.2.9.1.1.1.7. Pro: The story of [Utnapishtim](http://www.ancienttexts.org/library/mesopotamian/gilgamesh/tab11.htm) ends with Utnapishtim being blessed and made godlike. The story of Noah sort of ends with God blessing all life and putting his [bow in the clouds](http://inters.org/biblical-symbolism-rainbow) signifying that he will not use it to attack the Earth again.
1.6.2.2.9.1.1.2. Pro: The [story of Moses](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Exodus+2&version=NLT) is a re-telling of the story of [Sargon of Akkad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sargon_of_Akkad#Birth_legend). Moses lead his people out of Egypt using God's strength while Sargon established his kingdom in combat.

Because when Israel is lead by someone who [uses a stick to oppress his people](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=1+Kings+12&version=NIV) eventually "[blood is spread from one side of Jerusalem to the other](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=2+Kings+21&version=NIV)". 1.8.4.3. Con: Fasting does not show how poverty is, since when people live in poverty they don't know for certain that there will be food at sunset. Starvation until sunset is different from indefinite starvation. Those who fast are not being poor by starving until sunset.
1.8.4.4. Con: Fasting during Ramadan is very easy: those fasting can eat as much as they want from sunset to sunrise. Generally, people don't need to eat at night, as they had food during the day. Ramadan just reverses the timings from day to night.

This means that charity is not necessarily a good thing because it's possibly receiving more from the needy than it can justify from its spending on the needy \(maybe different needy\), particularly when a certain proportion of contributions goes to a religion's expenses, savings, and investments in buildings, paintings, sculptures etc.

1.10.11. Con: Superstitions, in general, have pragmatic value for human society - for example, scaring a child with stories of ghosts waiting in the darkness might have, on many occasion, saved the lives of children who'd be too scared to venture out alone in dangerous places. 1.11.9.4.3. Con: City-states in ancient [Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_education#Education_in_ancient_civilization) provided private education in literacy, arts and gymnastics for young boys \(from 7 to 14 years old\) mimicking modern formal schooling way before Christianity.
1.11.9.4.4. Con: Ancient [Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_education#Education_in_ancient_civilization) also developed forms of higher education where rich students could contniue their studies, learning rhetoric, mathematics, geography, natural history, politics, and logic.
1.11.9.4.4.1. Pro: In fact, the Hellenistic influence in modern education can be traced in the word [Lyceum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyceum), Aristotle's school named after its location, and a current terminology that many Western and Eastern countries still use.
1.11.9.4.5. Pro: Medieval universities started as [Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_education#Education_in_ancient_civilization) monastic schools and  modern systems of education in Europe derive from schools founded upon religious principles with the primary purpose of training the clergy.

Pro: During the [Middle Ages](https://www.britannica.com/topic/Western-philosophy/Medieval-philosophy), St. Augustine and St. Ambrose both studied earlier [philosophers](https://quatr.us/romans/roman-philosophy-ancient-rome.htm), assimilating Greek and Roman philosophy -the basis of Western thought- into Christian doctrine, trying to give a rational interpretation of Christian faith.

1.11.9.6.2. Pro: [Research](https://247wallst.com/special-report/2014/10/07/the-10-states-with-the-worst-quality-of-life/) in the US, shows that in most sociological measures of well-being, states with less levels or religion [fare better](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/the-secular-life/201410/secular-societies-fare-better-religious-societies) than more [religious](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/02/29/how-religious-is-your-state/?state=alabama) states.
1.11.9.6.2.1. Con: The correlation is the opposite than suggested above. Countries and states do not fare better because they lose their religiosity - they lose their religiosity when they find ways to establish functioning institutions to address the needs of their citizens who then no longer need to rely solely on hope and prayer.
1.11.9.6.2.1.1. Con: Therefore, religiosity is not necessary for societies' well-being if other secular and collective institutions are strong enough.
1.11.9.6.2.1.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.6.3.2.
1.11.9.6.2.1.2. Con: It is pure speculation to suggest that they lose religiosity only after having needs addressed so that prayer and hope need not be relied on. Prayer has been shown to be ineffective and hope need not be religious. The correlation is that as societies lose religiosity they become more successful, to suggest that the success causes the loss of religiosity is pure speculation. All we know is that success and lack of religion in this case go hand in hand.
1.11.9.6.2.2. Pro: There is a stark correlation between the 10 [most religious](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/02/29/how-religious-is-your-state/?state=alabama) states and the 10 [worst states](https://247wallst.com/special-report/2014/10/07/the-10-states-with-the-worst-quality-of-life/4/) in quality of life \(9 out of 10 coincidence\) and between the 10 [less religious](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/02/29/how-religious-is-your-state/?state=alabama) states and the [10 best one](https://www.usatoday.com/story/money/business/2014/10/11/24-7-wall-st-states-quality-of-life/16960973/)s \(7 out of 10 coincidence\).
1.11.9.6.2.3. Con: Correlation does not mean causation.
1.11.9.6.2.3.1. Pro: People living in poor and in conflict areas tend to be religious, because they need religion. They are not unsuccessful because they are religious, they are religious because they are unsuccessful.

Con: [Gallup](http://news.gallup.com/poll/142727/religiosity-highest-world-poorest-nations.aspx) and [Pew](http://www.pewresearch.org/methodology/international-survey-research/international-methodology/all-survey/all-country/all-year) polls, for instances, are made with large samples of respondents in each country who are asked if religion is important for them \(or in their lives\). Self-report surveys may be limited as research tools, but they do provide some reliable data and are used in a huge variety of fields.

Maybe societies are less religious because they are more economically successful.  The negative correlation between economic success and religiosity does not favor one conclusion over the other.

1.12. Pro: Religion is good for the psycho-social wellness of its followers.
1.12.1. Pro: Religion gives people's lives purpose and meaning.

1.12.1.2. Pro: Religion reminds people to look beyond mundane matters that seem important, including the material, personal obsessions, insecurities, and present sensibilities.
1.12.1.2.1. Con: Most people religious or otherwise find things more important than material obsessions and insecurities. Most people find interpersonal relationships to be important and helping others and loving others to be important. The only difference in this regard between the religious and the secular is that religious people also find supernatural pursuits to be important which has not been demonstrated to be beneficial.
1.12.1.2.2. Pro: Without religion, there would be only materialism, so people believe that the material world is all that exists.

1.12.1.4. Pro: Religion has been a good thing for humanity not only in terms of any beneficial side-effects of religion, but also as religion qua religion, i.e. it has been a good thing for humanity to search for - and maybe find - eternal meaning and ultimate reality.
1.12.1.4.1. Con: A lot of time has been spent searching for "eternal meaning and ultimate reality", much of it without positive results, either in terms of an actual result of the search or in terms of personal enlightenment resulting from the search itself.
1.12.1.5. Pro: A religious identity - whether theistic or [scientistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientism) - can provide goals to the lives of individuals and communities.
1.12.1.5.1. Con: [Goal setting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goal_setting) is an activity that has been studied in humans and is not religious. Though religion can give extra goals people can and do make their own goals regardless.

1.12.1.7. Pro: In a seemingly meaningless world, belief in a higher order helped people give meaning to their pleasure, and hope in suffering.
1.12.1.7.1. Pro: Religion helps people understand that they have been given a gift by God, their life, which can make them value it more and not see it as a random occurrence.
1.12.1.7.1.1. Con: The theory of evolution and our [place in the tree of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_evolution) is well established.

1.12.1.7.2. Con: Pleasure needs no added meaning as it is already by definition a good experience.

Many non-religious organisations and collectives provide the same opportunity to find purpose and meaning without the rituals and control around them.

1.12.4. Con: Religion has restricted people in enjoying the fullness of life because of "traditions" that doesn't make any sense
1.12.5. Pro: Some humans feel the need for rituals and religion is then a useful source.
1.12.5.1. Pro: Rituals [can help](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/why-rituals-work/) alleviate grief and boost confidence, as well as having an effect on our psychological processes.
1.12.5.1.1. Con: While rituals may be [important](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/donna-henes/rituals_b_3294412.html) there is no particular reason to connect them to an organised religion.
1.12.5.2. Pro: Rituals can show a commitment to shared values that can [bond](https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1007%2F978-3-658-10978-3_1) communities together.

1.12.6. Con: Religion, like any ideology or personal philosophy, can have positive and negative effects, dependent on the individual's use of such belief far more than the beliefs themselves.
1.12.7. Con: Religion usually requires prayer, and this is the part that has shown psychological usefulness. In reducing prayer to a psychological technique of objective visualisation, you remove the need for god. This kind of prayer can work without the use of god, for example the placebo effect, or sports visualisation techniques. So these ideas show that we don't need to pray to God in order for the the techniques to work.

1.12.10.2.1.5. Con: Judeo-Christian religions command their followers to treat their slaves fairly and with respect. Slavery was an ugly fact of life during the time, and religion helped make it less horrible.
1.12.10.2.1.5.1. Pro: [Exodus 21](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Exodus+21&version=NLT) is devoted to the fair treatment of slaves.
1.12.10.2.1.5.2. Pro: [Ephesians 6:5-9](http://biblehub.com/context/ephesians/6-5.htm) commands masters and slaves to treat each other  with good will.

1.12.10.2.1.5.3.1. Con: Even if slavery in the Bible was different chronologically and geographically, American Christian slaveholders often quoted several pro-slavery passages from the [Bible](http://time.com/5171819/christianity-slavery-book-excerpt/) to justify their practice.
1.12.10.2.1.5.3.1.1. Con: The whole practice of slavery was different in comparison to American Christian slaveholders. Slaves working under Hebrews were not murdered, beaten or abused and if they were it was taboo.
1.12.10.2.1.5.3.2. Pro: The Covenant Code dictated that if when slaves are significantly injured by their masters, manumission is to be the compensation given; the canonical examples mentioned are the knocking out of an eye or a tooth. [Exodus 21:26–27:26](http://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Exodus+21:26–27:26&version=nrsv). Americans slaveowners had no such laws.
1.12.10.2.1.5.3.3. Pro: The Deuteronomic Code forbids the people of Israel from handing over fugitive slaves to their masters or oppressing them, and instructs that these fugitives should be allowed to reside where they wish.

Although a literal reading would indicate that this applies to slaves of all nationalities and locations, the Mishnah and many commentators consider the rule to have the much narrower application, to just those slaves who flee from outside Israelite territory into it.[Deuteronomic Code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deuteronomic_Code)

[Slavery In The Bible](https://bibleapologetics.wordpress.com/slavery-in-the-bible-25/)

1.12.10.2.1.5.4.1. Con: Opposing slavery in those times would have been impossible. Religion likely led to the decline of slavery while ensuring the well-being and fair treatment of the slaves. Had abolition been pursued outright it would have been too extreme for the times and ignored.
1.12.10.2.1.5.4.1.1. Con: [Christianity early on](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome#Christianity_in_the_Roman_Empire) did away with many social conventions and refused to assimilate into Roman culture. Before that the Jews often went into [rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_wars) and refused to assimilate into local culture. These two religions based on that track record could have banned slavery amongst at the very least its own ranks.
1.12.10.2.1.5.4.2. Con: [Jeremiah 34:17](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jeremiah%2034:17&version=ESV) does explicitly condemn the practice of slavery, saying, "Therefore, thus says the Lord: You have not obeyed me by proclaiming liberty, every one to his brother and to his neighbor..."
1.12.10.2.1.5.4.2.1. Con: Upon reading the entire [passage](http://biblehub.com/nasb/jeremiah/34.htm) it is clear that it is only condemning the enslavement of fellow Israelites \(Hebrews\) and even then it allows them to be enslaved for a fixed amount of time as long as they are freed permanently afterwards.
1.12.10.2.1.5.5. Pro: Under Judaeo-Christian teachings, slavery becomes a contractual agreement between an employer and an employee. A rather strict contract, but the idea is no different. [Jewish](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Isaiah+58%3A6-7&version=ESV) [law](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Exodus+21%3A20&version=ESV) even prohibited buying and selling  [kidnapped people](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Exodus+21%3A16&version=ESV) into slavery and [returning escaped slaves](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Deuteronomy+23%3A15-16&version=ESV). [Christian](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Colossians+4%3A1&version=ESV) [teaching](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Ephesians+6%3A9&version=ESV) placed even more emphasis on the [fair treatment](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mark+10%3A42-45&version=ESV) of the [slaves](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Colossians+3%3A11&version=ESV).

1.18.2. Pro: In order to spread religion among the masses, organized religion has reduced subtle human pursuits such as "introspection" and "spirituality" into ritualistic activities to be performed mechanically, and sometimes performed purely to avoid committing "sin".
1.18.2.1. Pro: Praying to a god is by definition not introspection. It's either referring to an outside being or to just a part of oneself, depending on your religion.
1.18.2.1.1. Con: Referring to a part of oneself is the same as introspection.
1.18.2.2. Pro: Delaying introspection until particular times of day can't be good for the process. The impact of earlier occurrences will have dulled.
